<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Hygiene</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Series of practices performed to preserve health</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Hygienist" redirects here. For specific kinds of hygienist, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_hygienist" title="Industrial hygienist">Industrial hygienist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dental_hygienist" title="Dental hygienist">Dental hygienist</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For the social movement, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_hygiene" title="Social hygiene">Social hygiene</a>. For the community in the United States, see <a href="/wiki/Hygiene,_Colorado" title="Hygiene, Colorado">Hygiene, Colorado</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2575" data-file-width="2276" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg/220px-Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg/330px-Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg/440px-Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poster_%22Stop_microbes_use_good_hygiene%22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Poster to raise awareness about the importance of clean water for good hygiene, for use in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_countries" title="Islamic countries">Islamic countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><b>Hygiene</b> is a series of practices performed to preserve <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a>.
According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO), "Hygiene refers to conditions and practices that help to maintain health and prevent the spread of <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">diseases</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <b>Personal hygiene</b> refers to maintaining the body's cleanliness. Hygiene activities can be grouped into the following: home and everyday hygiene, personal hygiene, medical hygiene, sleep hygiene and <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">food hygiene</a>. Home and every day hygiene includes <a href="/wiki/Hand_washing" title="Hand washing">hand washing</a>, respiratory hygiene, food hygiene at home, hygiene in the kitchen, hygiene in the bathroom, laundry hygiene and medical hygiene at home.
</p><p>Many people equate hygiene with 'cleanliness,' but hygiene is a broad term. It includes such personal habit choices as how frequently to take a shower or bath, wash hands, trim <a href="/wiki/Nail_(anatomy)" title="Nail (anatomy)">fingernails</a>, and wash clothes. It also includes attention to keeping surfaces in the home and workplace clean, including <a href="/wiki/Bathroom" title="Bathroom">bathroom</a> facilities. Some regular hygiene practices may be considered good <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habit_(psychology)" title="Habit (psychology)">habits</a> by the society, while the neglect of hygiene can be considered disgusting, disrespectful, or threatening.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_and_overview">Definition and overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition and overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OCD_handwash.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1728" decoding="async" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/OCD_handwash.jpg/220px-OCD_handwash.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/OCD_handwash.jpg/330px-OCD_handwash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/OCD_handwash.jpg/440px-OCD_handwash.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OCD_handwash.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Washing one's hands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3">[3]</a></sup> a form of hygiene, is the most effective way to prevent the spread of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_diseases" title="Infectious diseases">infectious diseases</a></div></div></div>
<p>Hygiene is a practice<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> related to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lifestyle_(sociology)" title="Lifestyle (sociology)">lifestyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleanliness" title="Cleanliness">cleanliness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>. In medicine and everyday life, hygiene practices are employed as preventive measures to reduce the incidence and spreading of germs leading to <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">disease</a>.
</p><p>Hygiene practices vary from one <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a> to another.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the manufacturing of food,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> pharmaceutical,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> cosmetic<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and other products, good hygiene is a critical component of <a href="/wiki/Quality_assurance" title="Quality assurance">quality assurance</a>.
</p><p>The terms cleanliness and hygiene are often used interchangeably, which can cause confusion. In general, hygiene refers to practices that prevent spread of disease-causing organisms. Cleaning processes (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Hand_washing" title="Hand washing">handwashing</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3">[3]</a></sup>) remove infectious microbes as well as dirt and soil, and are thus often the means to achieve hygiene.
</p><p>Other uses of the term are as follows: <i>body hygiene, <a href="/wiki/Personal_care" title="Personal care">personal hygiene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sleep_hygiene" title="Sleep hygiene">sleep hygiene</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_hygiene" title="Mental hygiene">mental hygiene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oral_hygiene" title="Oral hygiene">dental hygiene</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Occupational_hygiene" title="Occupational hygiene">occupational hygiene</a></i>, used in connection with <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_and_everyday_hygiene">Home and everyday hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Home and everyday hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_hygiene_overview">Home hygiene overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Home hygiene overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Home hygiene pertains to the hygiene practices that prevent or minimize the spread of disease at home and other everyday settings such as social settings, public transport, the workplace, public places, etc.
</p><p>Hygiene in a variety of settings plays an important role in preventing the spread of infectious diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globalburden_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-globalburden-9">[9]</a></sup> It includes procedures used in a variety of domestic situations such as hand hygiene, respiratory hygiene, food and water hygiene, general home hygiene (hygiene of environmental sites and surfaces), care of domestic animals, and home health care (the care of those who are at greater risk of infection).
</p><p>At present, these components of hygiene tend to be regarded as separate issues, although based on the same underlying microbiological principles. Preventing the spread of diseases means breaking the chain of infection transmission. Simply put, if the chain of infection is broken, infection cannot spread. "Targeted hygiene" is based on identifying the routes of pathogen spread in the home and introducing hygiene practices at critical times to break the chain of infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup> It is using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Probabilistic_risk_analysis" title="Probabilistic risk analysis">risk-based approach</a> based on Hazard Analysis Critical Control Point (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HACCP" title="HACCP">HACCP</a>).
</p><p>The main sources of infection in the home are people (who are carriers or are infected), foods (particularly raw foods), water, pets and domestic animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2012_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2012-11">[11]</a></sup> Sites that accumulate stagnant water—such as sinks, <a href="/wiki/Toilet" title="Toilet">toilets</a>, waste pipes, cleaning tools, face cloths, etc. readily support microbial growth and can become secondary reservoirs of infection, though species are mostly those that threaten "at risk" groups. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pathogens" title="Pathogens">Pathogens</a> (potentially infectious bacteria, viruses etc.—colloquially called "germs") are constantly shed from these sources via mucous membranes, feces, vomit, skin scales, etc. Thus, when circumstances combine, people are exposed, either directly or via food or water, and can develop an infection.
</p><p>The main "highways" for the spread of pathogens in the home are the hands, hand and food contact surfaces, and cleaning cloths and utensils (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Fecal%E2%80%93oral_route" title="Fecal–oral route">fecal-oral route of transmission</a>). Pathogens can also be spread via clothing and household linens, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Towels" title="Towels">towels</a>. Utilities such as toilets and wash basins, for example, were invented for dealing safely with human waste but still have risks associated with them. Safe disposal of human waste is a fundamental need; poor <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> is a primary cause of diarrhea disease in low income communities. Respiratory viruses and fungal spores are spread via the air.
</p><p>Good home hygiene means engaging in hygiene practices at critical points to break the chain of infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2012_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2012-11">[11]</a></sup> Because the "infectious dose" for some pathogens can be very small (10-100 viable units or even less for some viruses), and infection can result from direct transfer of pathogens from surfaces via hands or food to the mouth, nasal mucous or the eye, 'hygienic cleaning' procedures should be sufficient to eliminate pathogens from critical surfaces.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hand_washing">Hand washing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hand washing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3160" data-file-width="1960" decoding="async" height="355" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg/220px-Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg/330px-Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg/440px-Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hand_Hygiene_Sign_in_Public_Restroom.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hand Hygiene Sign in Public Restroom</div></div></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Hand_washing" title="Hand washing">Hand washing</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hand_washing&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Hand_washing" title="Hand washing">Hand washing</a> (or handwashing), also known as hand hygiene, is the act of cleaning one's <a href="/wiki/Hand" title="Hand">hands</a> with <a href="/wiki/Soap" title="Soap">soap or handwash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a> to remove <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>/<a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a>, dirt, grease, or other harmful and unwanted substances stuck to the hands. Drying of the washed hands is part of the process as wet and moist hands are more easily recontaminated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hand_washing_CDC2020Wash2_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hand_washing_CDC2020Wash2-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hand_washing_Huang2012_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hand_washing_Huang2012-13">[13]</a></sup> If soap and water are unavailable, <a href="/wiki/Hand_sanitizer" title="Hand sanitizer">hand sanitizer</a> that is at least 60% (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V/v" title="V/v">v/v</a>) <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(chemistry)" title="Alcohol (chemistry)">alcohol</a> in water can be used as long as hands are not visibly excessively dirty or greasy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hand_washing_Centers_for_Disease_Control_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hand_washing_Centers_for_Disease_Control-15">[15]</a></sup> Hand hygiene is central to preventing the spread of <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infectious diseases</a> in home and everyday life settings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hand_washing_hand_hygiene_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hand_washing_hand_hygiene-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) recommends washing hands for at least 20 seconds before and after certain activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hand_washing_:7_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hand_washing_:7-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hand_washing_:8_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hand_washing_:8-18">[18]</a></sup> These include the five critical times during the day where washing hands with soap is important to reduce <a href="/wiki/Fecal%E2%80%93oral_route" title="Fecal–oral route">fecal-oral transmission</a> of disease: after using the <a href="/wiki/Toilet_(room)" title="Toilet (room)">toilet</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Urination" title="Urination">urination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Defecation" title="Defecation">defecation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Menstrual_hygiene_management" title="Menstrual hygiene management">menstrual hygiene</a>), after cleaning a child's bottom (changing <a href="/wiki/Diaper" title="Diaper">diapers</a>), before feeding a child, before eating and before/after preparing food or handling raw meat, fish, or poultry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hand_washing_:2_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hand_washing_:2-19">[19]</a></sup></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_(5630907486).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_%285630907486%29.jpg/220px-Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_%285630907486%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_%285630907486%29.jpg/330px-Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_%285630907486%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_%285630907486%29.jpg/440px-Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_%285630907486%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Finished_UDDT_in_Pumpuentsa_(5630907486).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tippy tap for handwashing after using a <a href="/wiki/Urine-diverting_dry_toilet" title="Urine-diverting dry toilet">urine-diverting dry toilet</a> in Pumpuentsa, Ecuador</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Respiratory_hygiene">Respiratory hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Respiratory hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Correct respiratory and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hand_hygiene" title="Hand hygiene">hand hygiene</a> when coughing and sneezing reduces the spread of pathogens particularly during the <a href="/wiki/Cold" title="Cold">cold</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flu" title="Flu">flu</a> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globalburden_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-globalburden-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Carry tissues and use them to catch coughs and sneezes, or sneeze into your elbow</li>
<li>Dispose of tissues as soon as possible</li></ul>
<h3><span id="Hygiene_in_the_kitchen.2C_bathroom_and_toilet"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hygiene_in_the_kitchen,_bathroom_and_toilet">Hygiene in the kitchen, bathroom and toilet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hygiene in the kitchen, bathroom and toilet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Routine cleaning of hands, food,  sites and surfaces (such as <a href="/wiki/Toilet_seat" title="Toilet seat">toilet seats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flush_toilet" title="Flush toilet">flush</a> handles, door and tap handles, work surfaces, bath and basin surfaces) in the kitchen, <a href="/wiki/Bathroom" title="Bathroom">bathroom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toilet_(room)" title="Toilet (room)">toilet rooms</a> reduces the spread of pathogens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hygiene_procedures_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-hygiene_procedures-20">[20]</a></sup> The infection risk from <a href="/wiki/Flush_toilet" title="Flush toilet">flush toilets</a> is not high, provided they are properly maintained, although some splashing and <a href="/wiki/Aerosol" title="Aerosol">aerosol</a> formation can occur during flushing, particularly when someone has diarrhea. Pathogens can survive in the scum or scale left behind on baths, <a href="/wiki/Shower" title="Shower">showers</a>, and washbasins after washing and bathing.
</p><p>Thorough cleaning is important in preventing the spread of fungal infections. Molds can live on wall and floor tiles and on shower curtains. Mold can be responsible for infections, cause allergic responses, deteriorate/damage surfaces, and cause unpleasant odors. Primary sites of fungal growth are inanimate surfaces, including carpets and soft furnishings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cole2000_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cole2000-21">[21]</a></sup> Air-borne fungi are usually associated with damp conditions, poor ventilation, or closed air systems.
</p><p>Hygienic cleaning can be done through:
</p>
<ul><li>Mechanical removal (i.e., cleaning) using a <a href="/wiki/Soap" title="Soap">soap</a> or <a href="/wiki/Detergent" title="Detergent">detergent</a>. To be effective as a hygiene measure, this process must be followed by thorough rinsing under running water to remove pathogens from the surface.</li>
<li>Using a process or product that inactivates the pathogens in situ. Pathogen kill is achieved using a "micro-biocidal" product, i.e., a <a href="/wiki/Disinfectant" title="Disinfectant">disinfectant</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antibacterial" title="Antibacterial">antibacterial</a> product; <a href="/wiki/Hand_sanitizer" title="Hand sanitizer">waterless hand sanitizer</a>; or by application of heat.</li>
<li>In some cases combined pathogen removal with kill is used, e.g., laundering of clothing and household linens such as towels and bed linen.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Laundry_hygiene">Laundry hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Laundry hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Laundry" title="Laundry">Laundry</a> hygiene involves practices that prevent disease and its spread via soiled clothing and household linens such as towels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2011_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2011-22">[22]</a></sup> Items most likely to be contaminated with pathogens are those that come into direct contact with the body, e.g., underwear, personal towels, facecloths, nappies. Cloths or other fabric items used during food preparation, or for cleaning the toilet or cleaning up material such as feces or vomit are a particular risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2012_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2012-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Microbiological and epidemiological data indicates that clothing and household linens etc. are a risk factor for infection transmission in home and everyday life settings as well as institutional settings. The lack of quantitative data linking contaminated clothing to infection in the domestic setting makes it difficult to assess the extent of this risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2011_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2011-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2012_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2012-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-larson2004_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-larson2004-23">[23]</a></sup> It also indicates that risks from clothing and household linens are somewhat less than those associated with hands, hand contact and food contact surfaces, and cleaning cloths, but even so these risks need to be managed through effective laundering practices. In the home, this routine should be carried out as part of a multibarrier approach to hygiene which includes hand, food, respiratory and other hygiene practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2011_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2011-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2012_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2012-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-larson2004_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-larson2004-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>Infectious diseases risks from contaminated clothing etc. can increase significantly under certain conditions, e.g., in healthcare situations in hospitals, care homes and the domestic setting where someone has diarrhoea, vomiting, or a skin or wound infection. It increases in circumstances where someone has reduced immunity to infection.
</p><p>Hygiene measures, including laundry hygiene, are an important part of reducing spread of antibiotic resistant strains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reccom_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-reccom-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2013_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2013-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In the community, otherwise healthy people can become persistent skin carriers of <a href="/wiki/Methicillin-resistant_Staphylococcus_aureus" title="Methicillin-resistant Staphylococcus aureus">MRSA</a>, or faecal carriers of enterobacteria strains which can carry multi-antibiotic resistance factors (e.g. NDM-1 or ESBL-producing strains). The risks are not apparent until, for example, they are admitted to hospital, when they can become "self infected" with their own resistant organisms following a surgical procedure. As persistent nasal, skin or bowel carriage in the healthy population spreads "silently" across the world, the risks from resistant strains in both hospitals and the community increases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2013_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2013-25">[25]</a></sup> In particular the data indicates that clothing and household linens are a risk factor for spread of S. aureus (including MRSA and PVL-producing MRSA strains), and that effectiveness of laundry processes may be an important factor in defining the rate of community spread of these strains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2011_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2011-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bllomfield2006_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-bllomfield2006-27">[27]</a></sup> Experience in the United States suggests that these strains are transmissible within families and in community settings such as prisons, schools and sport teams. Skin-to-skin contact (including unabraded skin) and indirect contact with contaminated objects such as towels, sheets and sports equipment seem to represent the mode of transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomfield2011_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-bloomfield2011-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>During laundering, temperature and <a href="/wiki/Laundry_detergent" title="Laundry detergent">detergent</a> work to reduce microbial contamination levels on fabrics. Soil and microbes from fabrics are severed and suspended in the wash water. These are then "washed away" during the rinse and spin cycles. In addition to physical removal, micro-organisms can be killed by thermal inactivation which increases as the temperature is increased. Chemical inactivation of microbes by the surfactants and activated oxygen-based bleach used in detergents contributes to the hygiene effectiveness of laundering. Adding hypochlorite bleach in the washing process achieves inactivation of microbes. A number of other factors can contribute including drying and ironing.
</p><p>Drying laundry on a line in direct sunlight is known to reduce pathogens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013 the International Scientific Forum on Home Hygiene (IFH) reviewed some 30 studies of the hygiene effectiveness of laundering at temperatures ranging from room temperature to 70 °C, under varying conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> A key finding was the lack of standardization and control within studies, and the variability in test conditions between studies such as wash cycle time, number of rinses, etc. The consequent variability in the data (i.e., the reduction in contamination on fabrics) obtained, in turn makes it extremely difficult to propose guidelines for laundering with any confidence, based on currently available data. As a result, there is significant variability in the recommendations for hygienic laundering of clothing etc. given by different agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_hygiene_at_home">Medical hygiene at home</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Medical hygiene at home">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Medical hygiene pertains to the hygiene practices that prevents or minimizes disease and the spreading of disease in relation to administering medical care to those who are infected or who are more "at risk" of infection in the home. Across the world, governments are increasingly under pressure to fund the level of healthcare that people expect. Care of increasing numbers of patients in the community, including at home is one answer, but can be fatally undermined by inadequate infection control in the home. Increasingly, all of these "at-risk" groups are cared for at home by a carer who may be a household member who thus requires a good knowledge of hygiene. People with reduced immunity to infection, who are looked after at home, make up an increasing proportion of the population (currently up to 20%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globalburden_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-globalburden-9">[9]</a></sup> The largest proportion are the elderly who have co-morbidities, which reduce their immunity to infection. It also includes the very young, patients discharged from hospital, taking immuno-suppressive drugs or using invasive systems, etc. For patients discharged from hospital, or being treated at home special "medical hygiene" (see above) procedures may need to be performed for them e.g. catheter or dressing replacement, which puts them at higher risk of infection.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Antiseptic" title="Antiseptic">Antiseptics</a> may be applied to cuts, wounds abrasions of the skin to prevent the entry of harmful bacteria that can cause sepsis. Day-to-day hygiene practices, other than special medical hygiene procedures<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> are no different for those at increased risk of infection than for other family members. The difference is that, if hygiene practices are not correctly carried out, the risk of infection is much greater.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disinfectants_and_antibacterials_in_home_hygiene">Disinfectants and antibacterials in home hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Disinfectants and antibacterials in home hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><a href="/wiki/Disinfectant" title="Disinfectant">Chemical disinfectants</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> are products that kill <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pathogens" title="Pathogens">pathogens</a>. If the product is a disinfectant, the label on the product should say "disinfectant" or "kills" pathogens. Some commercial products, e.g. bleaches, even though they are technically disinfectants, say that they "kill pathogens" but are not actually labelled as "disinfectants". Not all disinfectants kill all types of pathogens. All disinfectants kill bacteria (called bactericidal). Some also kill fungi (fungicidal), bacterial spores (sporicidal) or viruses (virucidal).
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Antibacterial_soap" title="Antibacterial soap">antibacterial</a> product acts against bacteria in some unspecified way. Some products labelled "antibacterial" kill bacteria while others may contain a concentration of active ingredient that only prevents them from multiplying. It is, therefore, important to check whether the product label states that it "kills bacteria." An antibacterial is not necessarily anti-fungal or anti-viral unless this is stated on the label.
</p><p>The term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disinfection" title="Disinfection">sanitizer</a> has been used to define substances that both clean and disinfect. More recently this term has been applied to alcohol-based products that disinfect the hands (<a href="/wiki/Hand_sanitizer" title="Hand sanitizer">alcohol hand sanitizers</a>). Alcohol hand sanitizers however are not considered to be effective on soiled hands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term <a href="/wiki/Biocide" title="Biocide">biocide</a> is a broad term for a substance that kills, inactivates or otherwise controls living organisms. It includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiseptics" title="Antiseptics">antiseptics</a> and disinfectants, which combat micro-organisms, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pesticides" title="Pesticides">pesticides</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_hygiene">Personal hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regular_activities">Regular activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Regular activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kulturbeutel1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kulturbeutel1.jpg/220px-Kulturbeutel1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kulturbeutel1.jpg/330px-Kulturbeutel1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kulturbeutel1.jpg/440px-Kulturbeutel1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kulturbeutel1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A clear plastic <a href="/wiki/Toiletry_bag" title="Toiletry bag">toiletry bag</a></div></div></div>
<p>Personal hygiene involves those practices performed by an individual to care for one's bodily health and wellbeing through cleanliness. Motivations for personal hygiene practice include reduction of personal illness, healing from personal illness, optimal health and sense of wellbeing, social acceptance and prevention of spread of illness to others. What is considered proper personal hygiene can be cultural-specific and may change over time.
</p><p>Practices that are generally considered proper hygiene include showering or bathing regularly, <a href="/wiki/Hand_washing" title="Hand washing">washing hands</a> regularly and especially before handling food, washing scalp hair, keeping hair short or removing hair, wearing clean clothing, brushing teeth, trimming fingernails and toenails, besides other practices. Some practices are gender-specific, such as by a woman during her <a href="/wiki/Menstruation" title="Menstruation">menstruation</a>. <a href="/wiki/Toiletry_bag" title="Toiletry bag">Toiletry bags</a> hold body hygiene and toiletry supplies.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Anal_hygiene" title="Anal hygiene">Anal hygiene</a> is the practice that a person performs on the anal area of themselves after <a href="/wiki/Defecation" title="Defecation">defecation</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Anus" title="Anus">anus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buttocks" title="Buttocks">buttocks</a> may be either washed with liquids or wiped with <a href="/wiki/Toilet_paper" title="Toilet paper">toilet paper</a> or adding <a href="/wiki/Gel_wipe" title="Gel wipe">gel wipe</a> to toilet tissue as an alternative to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wet_wipes" title="Wet wipes">wet wipes</a> or other solid materials in order to remove remnants of <a href="/wiki/Human_feces" title="Human feces">feces</a>.
</p><p>People tend to develop a routine for attending to their personal hygiene needs. Other personal hygienic practices would include covering one's mouth when coughing, disposal of soiled tissues appropriately, making sure toilets are clean, and making sure food handling areas are clean, besides other practices. Some cultures do not kiss or shake hands to reduce transmission of bacteria by contact.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Personal_grooming" title="Personal grooming">Personal grooming</a> extends personal hygiene as it pertains to the maintenance of a good personal and public appearance, which need not necessarily be hygienic. It may involve, for example, using deodorants or perfume, shaving, or combing, besides other practices.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hygiene_of_internal_ear_canals">Hygiene of internal ear canals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hygiene of internal ear canals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Earwax" title="Earwax">Earwax</a></div>
<p>Excessive cleaning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ear_canals" title="Ear canals">ear canals</a> can result in infection or irritation. The ear canals require less care than other parts of the body because they are sensitive and mostly self-cleaning; that is, there is a slow and orderly migration of the skin lining the ear canal from the eardrum to the outer opening of the ear. Old earwax is constantly being transported from the deeper areas of the ear canal out to the opening where it usually dries, flakes, and falls out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Attempts to clean the ear canals through the removal of <a href="/wiki/Earwax" title="Earwax">earwax</a> can push debris and foreign material into the ear that the natural movement of ear wax out of the ear would have removed.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oral_hygiene">Oral hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Oral hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oral_hygiene" title="Oral hygiene">Oral hygiene</a></div>
<p>It is recommended that all healthy adults brush twice a day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> softly,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> with the correct technique, replacing their toothbrush every few months (~3) or after a bout of illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5136" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg/220px-1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg/330px-1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg/440px-1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1st_Dental_Battalion_teaches_children_good_dental_hygeine_160223-M-QB247-008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Teaching a child how to properly brush the teeth</div></div></div>
<p>There are a number of common oral hygiene misconceptions. The <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">National Health Service (NHS) of England</a> recommends not rinsing the mouth with water after brushing — only to spit out excess <a href="/wiki/Toothpaste" title="Toothpaste">toothpaste</a>. They claim that this helps <a href="/wiki/Fluoride" title="Fluoride">fluoride</a> from toothpaste bond to teeth for its preventative effects against tooth decay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> It is also not recommended to brush immediately after drinking acidic substances, including sparkling water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> It is also recommended to floss once a day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> with a different piece of floss at each flossing session. The effectiveness of <a href="/wiki/Amorphous_calcium_phosphate" title="Amorphous calcium phosphate">amorphous calcium phosphate</a> products, such as Tooth Mousse, is in debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Visits to a dentist for a checkup every year at least are recommended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sleep_hygiene">Sleep hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sleep hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sleep_hygiene" title="Sleep hygiene">Sleep hygiene</a></div>
<p>Sleep hygiene is the recommended behavioral and environmental practice that is intended to promote better quality sleep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SH2014_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-SH2014-45">[45]</a></sup> This recommendation was developed in the late 1970s as a method to help people with mild to moderate <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a>, but, as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the evidence for effectiveness of individual recommendations is "limited and inconclusive".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SH2014_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-SH2014-45">[45]</a></sup> Clinicians assess the sleep hygiene of people who present with insomnia and other conditions, such as depression, and offer recommendations based on the assessment. Sleep hygiene recommendations include establishing a regular sleep schedule, using naps with care, not exercising physically or mentally too close to bedtime, limiting worry, limiting exposure to light in the hours before sleep, getting out of bed if sleep does not come, not using the bed for anything but sleep and avoiding <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Nicotine" title="Nicotine">nicotine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caffeine" title="Caffeine">caffeine</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Stimulant" title="Stimulant">stimulants</a> in the hours before bedtime and having a peaceful, comfortable and dark sleep environment.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_care_services_hygiene">Personal care services hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Personal care services hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Personal care services hygiene pertains to the practices related to the care and use of instruments used in the administration of personal care services to people:
</p><p>Personal care hygiene practices include:
</p>
<ul><li>Sterilization of instruments used by service providers including <a href="/wiki/Hairdresser" title="Hairdresser">hairdressers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esthetician" title="Esthetician">aestheticians</a>, and other service providers.</li>
<li>Sterilization by <a href="/wiki/Autoclave" title="Autoclave">autoclave</a> of instruments used in <a href="/wiki/Body_piercing" title="Body piercing">body piercing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tattoo" title="Tattoo">tattoo marking</a>.</li>
<li>Cleaning hands.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Challenges">Challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Excessive body hygiene is a possible sign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obsessive_compulsive_disorder" title="Obsessive compulsive disorder">obsessive compulsive disorder</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hygiene_hypothesis_and_allergies">Hygiene hypothesis and allergies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hygiene hypothesis and allergies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hygiene_hypothesis" title="Hygiene hypothesis">Hygiene hypothesis</a></div>
<p>Although media coverage of the <a href="/wiki/Hygiene_hypothesis" title="Hygiene hypothesis">hygiene hypothesis</a> has declined, a strong 'collective mindset' has become established that dirt is 'healthy' and hygiene somehow 'unnatural'. This has caused concern among health professionals that everyday life hygiene behaviors, which are the foundation of public health, are being undermined. In response to the need for effective hygiene in home and everyday life settings, the International Scientific Forum on Home Hygiene has developed a "risk-based" or targeted approach to home hygiene that seeks to ensure that hygiene measures are focused on the places, and at the times most critical for infection transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup> Whilst targeted hygiene was originally developed as an effective approach to hygiene practice, it also seeks, as far as possible, to sustain "normal" levels of exposure to the microbial flora of our environment to the extent that is important to build a balanced immune system.
</p><p>Although there is substantial evidence that some microbial exposures in early childhood can in some way protect against allergies, there is no evidence that humans need exposure to harmful microbes (infection) or that it is necessary to develop a clinical infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hh_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-hh-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hhsummary_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-hhsummary-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tooclean_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-tooclean-48">[48]</a></sup> Nor is there evidence that hygiene measures such as hand washing, food hygiene etc. are linked to increased susceptibility to <a href="/wiki/Atopy" title="Atopy">atopic disease</a>. If this is the case, there is no conflict between the goals of preventing infection and minimizing allergies. A consensus is now developing among experts that the answer lies in more fundamental changes in lifestyle etc. that have led to decreased exposure to certain microbial or other species, such as helminths, that are important for development of immuno-regulatory mechanisms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rook2010_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rook2010-49">[49]</a></sup> There is still much uncertainty as to which lifestyle factors are involved.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_hygiene">Medical hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Medical hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Medical hygiene pertains to the hygiene practices related to the administration of <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> and medical care that prevents or minimizes the spread of disease.
</p><p>Medical hygiene practices include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Isolation_(health_care)" title="Isolation (health care)">Isolation</a> of infectious persons or materials to prevent spread of infection.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sterilization_(microbiology)" title="Sterilization (microbiology)">Sterilization</a> of instruments used in <a href="/wiki/Surgery" title="Surgery">surgical procedures</a>.</li>
<li>Proper <a href="/wiki/Bandage" title="Bandage">bandaging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dressing_(medical)" title="Dressing (medical)">dressing</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Injuries" title="Injuries">injuries</a>.</li>
<li>Safe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waste_disposal" title="Waste disposal">disposal</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hazardous_waste" title="Hazardous waste">medical waste</a>.</li>
<li>Disinfection of reusables (i.e., linen, pads, uniforms).</li>
<li>Scrubbing up, <a href="/wiki/Hand_washing" title="Hand washing">handwashing</a>, especially in an operating room, but in more general health-care settings as well, where diseases can be transmitted.</li>
<li>Ethanol-based sanitizers.</li></ul>
<p>Most of these practices were developed in the 19th century and were well established by the mid-20th century. Some procedures (such as disposal of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_waste" title="Medical waste">medical waste</a>) were refined in response to late-20th century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disease_outbreaks" title="Disease outbreaks">disease outbreaks</a>, notably <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ebola" title="Ebola">Ebola</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_hygiene">Food hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Food hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">Food safety</a></div><p>
Culinary hygiene (or food hygiene) pertains to the practices related to food management and cooking to prevent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_contaminants" title="Food contaminants">food contamination</a>, prevent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_poisoning" title="Food poisoning">food poisoning</a> and minimize the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disease_transmission" title="Disease transmission">transmission of disease</a> to other foods, humans or animals. Culinary hygiene practices specify safe ways to handle, store, prepare, serve, and eat food.</p><div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">Food safety</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Food_safety&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">Food safety</a> (or food hygiene) is used as a scientific method/discipline describing handling, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">preparation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Food_storage" title="Food storage">storage of food</a> in ways that prevent <a href="/wiki/Foodborne_illness" title="Foodborne illness">food-borne illness</a>. The occurrence of two or more cases of a similar illness resulting from the ingestion of a common food is known as a food-borne disease outbreak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> This includes a number of routines that should be followed to avoid potential <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health hazards</a>. In this way, food safety often overlaps with <a href="/wiki/Food_defense" title="Food defense">food defense</a> to prevent harm to consumers. The tracks within this line of thought are safety between industry and the market and then between the market and the consumer. In considering industry to market practices, food safety considerations include the origins of food including the practices relating to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_labelling_regulations" title="Food labelling regulations">food labeling</a>, food hygiene, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_additives" title="Food additives">food additives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pesticide_residue" title="Pesticide residue">pesticide residues</a>, as well as policies on <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> and food and guidelines for the management of governmental <a href="/wiki/Import" title="Import">import</a> and <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">export</a> inspection and <a href="/wiki/Certification" title="Certification">certification</a> systems for foods. In considering market to consumer practices, the usual thought is that food ought to be safe in the market and the concern is safe delivery and preparation of the food for the consumer.</div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hygiene_aspects_in_low_and_middle_income_countries">Hygiene aspects in low and middle income countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hygiene aspects in low and middle income countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water,_sanitation_and_hygiene" title="Water, sanitation and hygiene">Water, sanitation and hygiene</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> (or low and middle income countries), universal access to water and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a>, coupled with hygiene promotion is essential in reducing infectious diseases. This approach has been integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_6" title="Sustainable Development Goal 6">Sustainable Development Goal Number 6</a> whose second target states: "By 2030, achieve access to adequate and equitable sanitation and hygiene for all and end <a href="/wiki/Open_defecation" title="Open defecation">open defecation</a>, paying special attention to the needs of women and girls and those in vulnerable situations".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SDG6_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-SDG6-51">[51]</a></sup> Due to their close linkages, water, sanitation, hygiene are together abbreviated and funded under the term <a href="/wiki/WASH" title="WASH">WASH</a> in <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development cooperation</a>.
</p><p>About 2 million people die every year due to diarrheal diseases, most of them are children less than 5 years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2008_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2008-52">[52]</a></sup> The most affected are the populations in developing countries, living in extreme conditions of poverty, normally peri-urban dwellers or rural inhabitants. Providing access to sufficient quantities of safe water, the provision of facilities for a sanitary disposal of excreta, and introducing sound hygiene behaviors are of capital importance to reduce the burden of disease caused by these risk factors.
</p><p>Research shows that, if widely practiced, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hand_washing_with_soap" title="Hand washing with soap">hand washing with soap</a> could reduce diarrhea by almost fifty percent<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2003_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2003-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aiello2008_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aiello2008-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fewtrell2005_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fewtrell2005-55">[55]</a></sup> and respiratory infections by nearly twenty-five percent<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WELLfactsheet_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-WELLfactsheet-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jefferson_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jefferson-57">[57]</a></sup> Hand washing with soap also reduces the incidence of skin diseases,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luby2005_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Luby2005-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luby2002_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Luby2002-59">[59]</a></sup> eye infections like trachoma and intestinal worms, especially <a href="/wiki/Ascariasis" title="Ascariasis">ascariasis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trichuriasis" title="Trichuriasis">trichuriasis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ashmudd_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-ashmudd-60">[60]</a></sup> Other hygiene practices, such as safe disposal of waste, surface hygiene, and care of domestic animals, are important in low income communities to break the chain of infection transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guidelines_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cleaning of <a href="/wiki/Toilet" title="Toilet">toilets</a> and hand wash facilities is important to prevent odors and make them socially acceptable. Social acceptance is an important part of encouraging people to use toilets and wash their hands, in situations where <a href="/wiki/Open_defecation" title="Open defecation">open defecation</a> is still seen as a possible alternative, e.g. in rural areas of some developing countries.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Household_water_treatment_and_safe_storage">Household water treatment and safe storage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Household water treatment and safe storage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg/220px-Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg/330px-Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg/440px-Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia-sodis-gross.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Solar_water_disinfection" title="Solar water disinfection">Solar water disinfection (SODIS)</a> application in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> using clear <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene_terephthalate" title="Polyethylene terephthalate">polyethylene terephthalate (PET)</a> plastic beverage bottles</div></div></div>
<p>Household water treatment and safe storage ensure drinking water is safe for consumption. These interventions are part of the approach of <a href="/wiki/Self-supply_of_water_and_sanitation" title="Self-supply of water and sanitation">self-supply of water</a> for households.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">Drinking water quality</a> remains a significant problem in developing<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2007_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2007-62">[62]</a></sup> and in developed countries;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFHhhwater_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-IFHhhwater-63">[63]</a></sup> even in the European region it is estimated that 120 million people do not have access to <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">safe drinking water</a>. Point-of-use water quality interventions can reduce diarrheal disease in communities where water quality is poor or in emergency situations where there is a breakdown in water supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2007_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2007-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFHhhwater_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-IFHhhwater-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clasen2008_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clasen2008-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who2005-wateremergenciesdisasters_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-who2005-wateremergenciesdisasters-65">[65]</a></sup>
Since water can become contaminated during storage at home (e.g. by contact with contaminated hands or using dirty storage vessels), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Household_water_storage" title="Household water storage">safe storage of water</a> in the home is important.
</p><p>Methods for treatment of drinking water at the household level include:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hygiene_procedures_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-hygiene_procedures-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who2005-wateremergenciesdisasters_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-who2005-wateremergenciesdisasters-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>Chemical disinfection using chlorine or iodine</li>
<li>Boiling</li>
<li>Filtration using ceramic filters</li>
<li>Solar disinfection – Solar disinfection is an effective method, especially when no chemical disinfectants are available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li>UV irradiation – community or household UV systems may be batch or flow-though. The lamps can be suspended above the water channel or submerged in the water flow.</li>
<li>Combined flocculation/disinfection systems – available as sachets of powder that act by coagulating and flocculating sediments in water followed by release of chlorine.</li>
<li>Multibarrier methods – Some systems use two or more of the above treatments in combination or in succession to optimize efficacy.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portable_water_purification" title="Portable water purification">Portable water purification</a> devices</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2526" data-file-width="2014" decoding="async" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg/210px-Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg/315px-Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg/420px-Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stamnos_women_bath_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_2411.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Three young women bathing, 440–430 BCE. Ancient Greece.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-,_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten,_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-%2C_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten%2C_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg/220px-Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-%2C_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten%2C_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-%2C_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten%2C_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg/330px-Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-%2C_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten%2C_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-%2C_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten%2C_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg/440px-Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-%2C_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten%2C_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katalog_vintern_1905-1906._AB_Nordiska_Kompaniet._H%C3%A5r-,_Toalett-_%26_Tandvatten,_Pomada_%26_Brilliantine_-_Nordiska_Museet_-_NMA.0040796.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Swedish advert for toiletries, 1905–1906.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Public_health#History" title="Public health">Public health § History</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_water_supply_and_sanitation" title="History of water supply and sanitation">History of water supply and sanitation</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bathing culture in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_literature" title="Chinese literature">Chinese literature</a> can be traced back to the <a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang dynasty</a> (1600–1046 BCE), where <a href="/wiki/Oracle_bone" title="Oracle bone">Oracle bone</a> inscriptions describe people washing their hair and body in a bath, suggesting people paid attention to personal hygiene. The <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Rites" title="Book of Rites">Book of Rites</a></i>, a work regarding <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> (1046–256 BCE) ritual, politics, and culture compiled during the <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a>, describes that people should take a hot shower every five days, and wash their hair every three days. It was also considered good manners to take a bath provided by the host before a <a href="/wiki/Dinner" title="Dinner">dinner</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a>, bathing became a regular activity and for government officials, bathing was required every five days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-woc_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-woc-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ancient bath facilities have been found in ancient Chinese cities, such as Dongzhouyang archaeological site in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henan_Province" title="Henan Province">Henan Province</a>. Bathrooms were called <span title="Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="zh-Latn">Bi</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">湢</span>), and bathtubs were made of bronze or timber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vc_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-vc-68">[68]</a></sup> Bath beans – a powdery soap mixture of ground beans, cloves, eaglewood, flowers, and even powdered jade – were recorded in the Han Dynasty. Bath beans were considered luxury toiletries, while common people simply used powered beans without spices mixed in. Luxurious bathhouses built around hot springs were recorded in <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-woc_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-woc-67">[67]</a></sup> While royal bathhouses and bathrooms were common among ancient Chinese nobles and commoners, public bathhouses were a relatively late development. In the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> (960–1279), public bathhouses became popular and people could find them everywhere on the street,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vc_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-vc-68">[68]</a></sup> and bathing became an essential part of social life and recreation. Bathhouses often provided massage, nail cut service, rubdown service, ear cleaning, food and beverages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vc_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-vc-68">[68]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a>, who traveled to China during the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a>, noted Chinese bathhouses were using <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> to heat the bathhouse, which he had never seen before in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Coal was so plentiful that Chinese people of every social class had bathrooms in their houses, and people took showers everyday in the winter for enjoyment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>A typical <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> bathhouse had slabbed floors and brick domed ceilings. A huge boiler would be installed in the back of the house, connected with the bathing pool through a tunnel. Water could be pumped into the pool by <a href="/wiki/Water_wheel" title="Water wheel">turning wheels</a> attended by the staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vc_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-vc-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The origin of Japanese bathing is <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Misogi" title="Misogi">misogi</a></i></span>, ritual purification with water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clark1994_backcover_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clark1994_backcover-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Heian_period" title="Heian period">Heian period</a> (794–1185), houses of prominent families, such as the families of court nobles or samurai, had baths. The bath had lost its religious significance and instead became leisure. <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Misogi</i></span> became <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">gyōzui</i></span>, to bathe in a shallow wooden tub.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clark1994_p.36_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clark1994_p.36-73">[73]</a></sup> In the 17th century, the first European visitors to Japan recorded the habit of daily baths in mixed sex groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clark1994_backcover_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clark1994_backcover-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Indian subcontinent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The earliest written account of Elaborate codes of hygiene can be found in several Hindu texts, such as the <a href="/wiki/Manusmriti" title="Manusmriti">Manusmriti</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vishnu_Purana" title="Vishnu Purana">Vishnu Purana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Bathing is one of the five <a href="/wiki/Nitya_karma" title="Nitya karma">Nitya karmas</a> (daily duties) in Hinduism, and not performing it leads to sin, according to some scriptures.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ayurveda" title="Ayurveda">Ayurveda</a> is a system of medicine developed in ancient times that is still practiced in India, mostly combined with conventional Western medicine. Contemporary Ayurveda stresses a <a href="/wiki/Sattvic_diet" title="Sattvic diet">sattvic diet</a> and good digestion and <a href="/wiki/Excretion" title="Excretion">excretion</a>. Hygiene measures include <a href="/wiki/Oil_pulling" title="Oil pulling">oil pulling</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tongue_scraping" title="Tongue scraping">tongue scraping</a>. Detoxification also plays an important role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Americas">The Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hygiene&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: The Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
